## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: nonlinear oscillator dynamics
**Analysis**: This task seeks the acceleration equation for a nonlinear harmonic oscillator. The acceleration dv_dt typically depends on position x (restoring force), velocity v (damping), and possibly time t (external driving), with nonlinear terms in x and/or v distinguishing it from a simple harmonic oscillator.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * x**2 * v (nonlinear damping)
- Driven oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (periodic external forcing)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (forced nonlinear oscillator)
- Rayleigh oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v**3 (velocity-cubed nonlinear damping)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * x**2) (amplitude-dependent frequency)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * (1 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) (time-modulated stiffness)
- Coulomb + viscous damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * (v**2 + c3)**(-0.5) (mixed damping model)
- Nonlinear pendulum approximation: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (exact pendulum restoring torque)
- Generalized nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * x * v**2 (mixed nonlinear terms)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) → symmetric potential well, preserves x → -x symmetry
- Terms like x²*v indicate amplitude-dependent damping → van der Pol type self-excitation or limit cycles
- Sinusoidal time dependence sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) → external periodic driving force
- Cubic position term x³ with same sign as linear term → hardening spring; opposite sign → softening spring
- Velocity-dependent terms with odd powers (v, v³) → dissipative effects; even powers (v²) → conservative nonlinearity
- Product terms x*cos(c*t) → parametric excitation, can lead to parametric resonance
- Absence of explicit time dependence → autonomous system, energy-based analysis applies
- sin(c*x) as restoring force → pendulum-like large-amplitude oscillations with bounded potential

I need to determine if any candidate formula can match the GT:

**GT:** `-0.752289977167006*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Expanding: `0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.752289977167006*v - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Simplifying: `-1.1598282332023*x**3 - 1.36630597420348*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x))`

So the GT has four terms:
1. `c*x**3`
2. `c*v`
3. `c*v*x**2`
4. `c*v*exp(-|x|)`

The critical term is `v*exp(-|x|)`. This involves `exp(-|x|)`, which is an even function with a cusp at x=0.

Now I need to check which candidates can reproduce `v*exp(-|x|)`.

**Key analysis of exp(-|x|):** This function is NOT equivalent to `exp(c*x)*cos(c*x)`, `exp(c*x**2)`, `log(c*exp(c*x)+1)`, or any smooth function of x. The absolute value creates a non-differentiable point at x=0.

Let me check candidates with `log(c4*exp(c5*x) + 1)`:
Note that `log(exp(ax) + 1)` is the softplus function. For large negative x, it approaches 0; for large positive x, it approaches ax. This is NOT symmetric like exp(-|x|).

However, consider: Can we combine `c1*v + c3*v*log(c4*exp(c5*x) + 1)` to approximate `v*exp(-|x|)`? No — `log(c*exp(ax)+1)` is monotonic in x, while `exp(-|x|)` is symmetric (even function). No combination of polynomial terms in x and a single softplus can create exp(-|x|).

What about candidates with `exp(c*x)*cos(c*x)`? This is also not equivalent to `exp(-|x|)` — it's smooth and oscillatory.

What about `exp(c*sin(c*x + c))`? With appropriate parameters, `sin(c*x+c)` could potentially approximate `|x|` locally but not globally.

**Candidate 40:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*v*x**2 + c3*v*x**2*Abs(x) + c4*v*exp(c5*sin(c6*x + c7)) + c8*x + c9*v*x`
Has `Abs(x)` but in `x**2*|x| = |x|**3 = x**2*|x|`, not `exp(-|x|)`.

**Candidate 12:** `c0*x**3 + c1*v + c2*v*x**2 + c3*v*exp(c4*x)*cos(c5*x) + c6*v*Abs(x)`
Has `v*Abs(x)` but we need `v*exp(-|x|)`, not `v*|x|`.

None of the candidates contain `exp(-Abs(x))` or an equivalent expression. The term `v*exp(-|x|)` is a very specific non-smooth function that cannot be reproduced by any of the smooth building blocks (polynomials, exp(smooth), cos(smooth), log(smooth), sin(smooth)) available in the candidates.

Even candidates with multiple terms cannot combine smooth functions to produce the non-analytic behavior of `exp(-|x|)` at x=0.

After carefully reviewing all 53 candidates, none of them contain the essential `exp(-|x|)` term or any combination that could replicate it exactly.

I need to compare each candidate against the Ground Truth (GT):

**GT numerical expression:** `-0.752289977167006*v*(1 - x**2) - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-Abs(x)) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Since x is strictly positive on this benchmark, `Abs(x) = x`, so:
`-0.752289977167006*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.61401597703647*v - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-x) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

Combining v terms:
`-1.36630595420348*v + 0.752289977167006*v*x**2 - 0.307007988518235*v*exp(-x) - 1.1598282332023*x**3`

So GT = `c_a*x**3 + c_b*v + c_c*v*x**2 + c_d*v*exp(-x)`

where c_a = -1.1598..., c_b = -1.3663..., c_c = 0.7523..., c_d = -0.3070...

The key basis functions are: **x³, v, v·x², v·exp(-x)**

Now I need to check which candidates can express `v*exp(-x)` using their terms.

**Key identity:** `log(c4*exp(c5*x) + 1)` with c5 < 0 and appropriate c4... For large negative c5*x, this approaches 0; for large positive c5*x, it approaches c5*x. This is a softplus function and is NOT equivalent to exp(-x) for any constants. However, if we set c5 = -1 and c4 = 1: `log(exp(-x) + 1)` which is NOT the same as `exp(-x)`.

**Key identity:** `exp(c4*x)*cos(c5*x)` with c5 = 0 gives `exp(c4*x)`. Setting c4 = -1 gives `exp(-x)`. ✓

So candidates with `v*exp(c4*x)*cos(c5*x)` can match by setting c5 = 0, c4 = -1.

Let me check candidates with `v*log(c4*exp(c5*x) + 1)`: This is a softplus-like function and cannot equal `exp(-x)` for all x. **These cannot match.**
